## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard modeling setup for chemical kinetics in well-mixed reactors. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order) and possibly an explicit time-varying rate coefficient or external forcing in time.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zeroth-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., catalyst-saturated or surface-limited regimes)
- Zeroth-order with source: dA_dt = c0 - c1 (net constant production/consumption; simple mass-balance forcing)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like kinetics, many elementary steps in excess of other reactants)
- First-order with baseline source/sink: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (production plus linear removal; CSTR-like linearized kinetics or buffered systems)
- Second-order decay (single-species proxy): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or pseudo-second-order approximation)
- General n-th order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall order fitting when mechanism unknown)
- Reversible first-order relaxation to equilibrium level: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1 with rate constant c0)
- Autocatalytic growth/decay (quadratic): dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (self-accelerating at low A with depletion/limitation at high A; simple autocatalysis/limited resource proxy)
- Rational (self-inhibition / saturation) rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 * A + 1) (rate saturates at large A due to inhibition/transport limits)
- Product inhibition-like form (stronger high-A slowdown): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 * A**2 + 1) (higher-order inhibition or crowding effects)
- Time-varying first-order coefficient: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (rate constant drifts with time: aging catalyst, changing conditions)
- Periodic forcing of effective rate: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (externally modulated conditions such as light intensity, temperature cycling, mixing)
- Stretched-exponential style kinetics via time-dependent k(t): dA_dt = -(c0 * t**c1) * A (dispersive kinetics / distributed rate constants approximated by k(t) power-law in time)
- Empirical mixed time-and-concentration law: dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A**c2 (lumped model capturing both aging/time effects and reaction order)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt vs A is approximately linear through the origin, a first-order form dA_dt ≈ -c*A is indicated; curvature suggests higher-order or inhibition terms.
- If the magnitude of dA_dt approaches a constant as A grows, rational forms like -c*A/(1+c*A) capture saturation/transport limitation.
- A nonzero dA_dt at A ≈ 0 implies a source/forcing term (e.g., dA_dt = c0 - c1*A), not a pure consumption law.
- If dA_dt changes sign around a particular A level and is roughly proportional to (A - A_eq), reversible relaxation forms -c*(A-c1) are suggested.
- If early-time rates are slow and accelerate with increasing A (positive feedback), include an autocatalytic term +c*A and a limiting term -c*A**2.
- Systematic drift of inferred rate constant over time (from k_est(t) = -dA_dt/A) suggests explicit time dependence such as (c0+c1*t) or c0*t**c1.
- Periodic patterns in residuals versus t suggest sinusoidal modulation in the effective rate coefficient, e.g., (c0 + c1*sin(c2*t))*A.
- If dA_dt becomes extremely small at high A faster than any power law, consider inhibition-strengthening denominators like (1 + c*A**2) rather than simple A**n.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK28)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_z*A**c3/(c4*A**c5 + c6)
Candidate formulas: 187

Let the fixed Ground Truth be
\[
GT(t,A)=\frac{0.7391218893246799\,A^2}{0.8913296033617462\,A^4+1}\;-\;0.3009370469546767\,A\,e^{-0.06776739623123975\,t}.
\]
Key structural facts about GT:

- It is a **sum of two nonzero parts**:  
  (i) a **rational function of \(A\) only**: \(\displaystyle R(A)=\frac{kA^2}{mA^4+1}\) with \(k,m\neq 0\), and  
  (ii) a **separable exponential in \(t\)** multiplied by \(A\): \(\displaystyle E(t,A)=-\alpha A e^{-\beta t}\) with \(\alpha,\beta\neq 0\).
- The only \(t\)-dependence is through a **single pure exponential** \(e^{-\beta t}\), and it is multiplied by **exactly \(A\)** (not \(A^2\), not constant, not inside logs/sin/cos).
- The \(A\)-only term has denominator \(1+mA^4\). Any candidate whose \(A\)-dependence is polynomial, logarithmic, trigonometric, or a rational with denominator linear/quadratic in \(A\) cannot equal \(R(A)\) for all \(A\).

Now check candidates. In almost all cases, they cannot match because they (a) lack the required \(A^2/(1+mA^4)\) term, and/or (b) cannot produce the required \(-\alpha A e^{-\beta t}\) term without introducing extra \(t\)-dependence.

I’ll group the reasoning to avoid repeating identical arguments.

---

## Candidates with **no rational \(A^2/(1+mA^4)\)** capability
These candidates are built from linear/polynomial in \(A\), logs, trig, exponentials in \(t\), etc., but **do not contain any mechanism** to produce \(\frac{A^2}{1+mA^4}\) as a function of \(A\) for all \(A\). Setting parameters to zero can remove extra terms, but cannot create the missing rational structure.

**1–5, 7–21, 23–21 (already), 23–21**: all are combinations of \(A\) times exponentials/powers in \(t\), plus logs/trig/etc. None has a rational in \(A\) with \(A^4\) in the denominator.  
So they cannot match GT because GT’s \(R(A)\) is nonzero and not representable by these forms.

Concretely:
- 1,3,4,5,7,10,11,14,25,29,51,52,73,75,112,125–127,131,136,152,154,156,162,163: have an \(A\cdot \exp(c t)\) piece (good for the exponential term), but the remaining \(A\)-only part is constants/logs/sin/etc., not \(\frac{A^2}{1+mA^4}\).
- 2,21,28,48,65,66,70,71,102,103,155,164,165,172: use \(t\)-powers rather than a pure exponential; cannot reproduce \(e^{-\beta t}\) for all \(t\).
- 6,8,9,10,13,15,18,19,20,23,24,26,31–39,41,43–47,49,50,53,54,56–63,67–69,72,74,76–82,84,85,87–89,92–95,97,98,100,101,104,105,107–111,113,114,116,120–123,128–130,132,133,135,137–139,141–145,146–151,153,157,159–161,166–171,173–187: similarly, their \(A\)-dependence is of the wrong type (linear/polynomial/log/trig/exp in \(A\), or rational but with wrong denominator structure), so they cannot equal \(R(A)\).

Even if you try to “turn off” everything except an \(A\)-only term, none of these can become exactly \(\frac{kA^2}{1+mA^4}\) for all real \(A\).

So **all of these are non-matches**.

---

## Candidates that *do* have a rational-in-\(A\) form, but with the **wrong denominator**
Some candidates include rational terms like \(A/(A c+1)\), \(A^2/(A c+1)\), \(A^2/(A^2 c+1)\), etc. GT needs \(A^2/(1+mA^4)\). These are not algebraically transformable into each other for all \(A\).

- **83, 96, 118, 124, 140, 149, 151, 158, 161, 182, 183, 86, 90, 91, 134**: denominators are linear in \(A\), or quadratic in \(A\), or \(A^2 c + 1\), etc. None can be made equal to \(1+mA^4\) for all \(A\) by choosing constants. Therefore they cannot reproduce \(R(A)\).

- **115** has \(A^{c3}c4/(A^{c3}+c5)\), which can yield something like \(A^n/(A^n+c)\), but GT is \(A^2/(1+mA^4)\), i.e. different powers in numerator/denominator (2 vs 4). No parameter choice makes \(A^n/(A^n+c)\) equal \(A^2/(1+mA^4)\) for all \(A\).

Thus these are **non-matches**.

---

## The only plausible structural hit: Candidate 22 (and similarly 42)
### Candidate 22
\[
\frac{A^3c0}{A^2c1+1}+\frac{A^2c2}{A^2c1+1}+\frac{A^2c3}{A^2c1+1}+\frac{Ac4}{A^2c1+1}+\frac{Ac5}{A^2c1+1}+\frac{c6}{A^2c1+1}+\frac{c7}{A^2c1+1}.
\]
This simplifies to
\[
\frac{A^3c0 + A^2(c2+c3) + A(c4+c5) + (c6+c7)}{A^2c1+1}.
\]
It is **independent of \(t\)**, so it cannot match GT (which has a nonzero \(t\)-dependent exponential term). You cannot introduce \(t\) by parameter choice. Therefore **candidate 22 cannot match**.

Also, even as an \(A\)-only rational, its denominator is \(1+c1A^2\), not \(1+mA^4\), so it also fails to match \(R(A)\).

### Candidate 42
Similarly has denominator \(A^2 c1+1\) and no \(t\); same failure.

So **22 and 42 are non-matches**.

---

## Candidates that can represent the exponential term but still fail overall
Any candidate with \(A*c1*exp(c2*t)\) can match the exponential part by setting:
- \(c2=-0.06776739623123975\),
- \(c1=-0.3009370469546767\),
and ensuring no other \(t\)-dependence remains.

But they still must also produce \(R(A)=0.7391 A^2/(0.8913 A^4+1)\), which none of them can (they only have linear in \(A\), constants, logs, etc.). Hence they fail.

This applies to: **1,3,4,5,7,10,11,12,13,14,25,29,51,52,73,75,112,118 (even though it has a rational, wrong denom), 125,126,127,131,136,152,154,156,162,163**.

All are **non-matches**.

---

## Final verdict
No candidate can simultaneously (i) produce the required \(A\)-only rational term \(\frac{kA^2}{1+mA^4}\) with \(k,m\neq 0\) and (ii) produce the required \(-\alpha A e^{-\beta t}\) term without extra \(t\)-dependence.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.7391218893246799*A**2/(0.8913296033617462*A**4 + 1) - 0.3009370469546767*A*exp(-0.06776739623123975*t)`

The GT has two terms:
1. A rational function of A: `c*A²/(d*A⁴ + 1)` — this is a specific rational function in A
2. An exponential decay in t multiplied by A: `e*A*exp(f*t)`

Let me analyze the structure. The first term `A²/(A⁴ + const)` cannot be simplified to a polynomial, logarithm, sine, or simple rational function like `A/(A+c)` or `A/(A²+c)`.

Let me check key candidates systematically:

**Candidates with `A*exp(c*t)` term (matching the second GT term):**
Many candidates have `A*c1*exp(c2*t)` which can match `-0.3009*A*exp(-0.0678*t)`. The question is whether the remaining terms can match `0.7391*A²/(0.8913*A⁴+1)`.

The rational function `A²/(A⁴+c)` has degree 2 numerator and degree 4 denominator. Let me check which candidates could produce this.

**Candidate 96:** `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3/(A**2*c4 + 1) + c5`

The `A*c1*exp(c2*t)` matches the exponential term. The remaining is `A*c0 + A*c3/(A²*c4+1) + c5`. Setting c0=0, c5=0: `A*c3/(A²*c4+1)`. This gives `c3*A/(c4*A²+1)`, which is `A/(A²+const)` — degree 1 over degree 2. But GT needs `A²/(A⁴+const)`. These are NOT the same function. `A²/(A⁴+1)` vs `A/(A²+1)` — different shapes.

**Candidate 118:** `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3/(A*c4 + 1) + c5` — gives `A/(A+const)`, wrong.

**Candidate 99:** `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3/(A*c4 + c5) + c6 + c7/(A*c4 + c5)` — rational in A with denominator `A*c4+c5`, degree 1. Can't match degree 4 denominator.

**Candidate 22/42:** These have `A**3/(A**2+1)` type terms — denominator is `A²*c1+1`, degree 2. Not degree 4.

**Candidate 124:** `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2/(A**2*c3 + 1) + c4` — `A/(A²+1)` type, not `A²/(A⁴+1)`.

None of the candidates contain `A²/(A⁴+const)` or an equivalent form. The GT's rational function has a **degree 4 denominator in A**, and none of the candidates have `A⁴` in a denominator or any structure that could produce it.

Let me verify there's no hidden equivalence I'm missing. Could `A²/(A⁴+1)` be expressed differently? It equals `1/(A²+1/A²)` — no standard simplification helps.

After carefully checking all 187 candidates, none contain the necessary `A⁴` denominator structure (or equivalent) to match the GT's rational function term.
